Types of Qiyas and Istihsan in Hanafi Usul
Definition and classification of qiyas and istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of qiyas and two types of istihsan and explain why istihsan is considered a preferred type of qiyas.

Core Idea
Istihsan is a stronger qiyas; effect overrides appearance.

Al-Bazdawi opens the chapter on Qiyas and Istihsan by classifying each into two types. This classification is foundational for understanding how Hanafi jurists prioritise legal reasoning. The key is that the strength of a ruling's effect (athar) determines preference, not the apparent clarity of the analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of qiyas
Read the first two sentences: one type has weak effect, the other has apparent corruption but hidden soundness and effect.
2
Identify the two types of istihsan
Read the next two sentences: one type has strong hidden effect, the other has apparent effect but hidden corruption.
3
Understand istihsan as a type of qiyas
The author states that istihsan is one of the two qiyases, but it is called istihsan to indicate it is the preferable face to act upon.
4
Note the legal rule for preference
The passage asserts that strength of effect (athar) is the criterion, not clarity. The example of the world vs. Hereafter illustrates this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب
القياس والاستحسان
وكل واحد منهما على وجهين :
أما أحد نوعي القياس : فما ضعف أثره.
والنوع الثاني : ما ظهر فساده واستترت صحته وأثره.
وأحد نوعي الاستحسان: ما قوي أثره وإن كان خفياً.
والثاني : ما ظَهَرَ أثره، وخفي فساده.
وإنما الاستحسان عندنا أحد القياسين، لكنه استحساناً؛ إشارةً سمي إلى أنه الوجه الأولى في العمل به وأن العمل بالآخر جائز، كما جاز
العمل بالطرد وإن كان الأثر أولى منه.
والاستحسان أقسام : وهو ما ثبت بالأثر، مثل السلم، والإجارة،
وبقاء الصوم مع فعل الناسي.
ومنه ما ثبت بالإجماع، وهو الاستصناع.
ومنه ما ثبت بالضرورة ، وهو تطهير الحياض والآبار والأواني.
وإنما غرضنا ها هنا تقسيم وجوه العلل في حق الأحكام، ولما صارت العلة عندنا علةً بأثرها : سمينا الذي ضعف أثرها: قياساً، وسمينا الذي قَوِيَ أَثرها استحساناً، أي قياساً مُستحسناً، وقدمنا الثاني وإن كان خفياً
على الأول وإن كان جلياً ؛ لأن العبرة لقوة الأثر، دون الظهور والجلاء. ألا يُرى أن الدنيا ظاهرة، والعقبى باطنة، وقد ترجح الباطن لقوة ، وهو الدوام والخلود والصَّفوة، وتأخر الظاهر لضعف أثره، القلب، والبصر مع العقل، فسقط حكم القياس بمعارضة
الأثر،
و كالنفس مع الاستحسان؛ لعدمه في التقدير.
سبع
مثال ذلك : أن سؤر سباع الطير في القياس : نجس؛ لأنه سؤر ما هو مطلق، فكان كسور سباع البهائم، وهذا معنى ظاهر الأثر؛ لأنهما سواء في حرمة الأكل، وفي الاستحسان هو طاهر ؛ لأن السبع ليس بنجس العين؛ بدليل جواز الانتفاع به شرعاً، وقد ثبتت نجاسته ضرورة تحريم لحمه، فأثبتنا حكماً بین حكمين، وهو النجاسة المجاورة، فثبتت صفة النجاسة في رطوبته ولعابه، وسباعُ الطير تشرب بالمنقار على سبيل
الأخذ، ثم الابتلاع ، والعَظمُ طاهر بذاته، خال عن مجاورة النَّجَس. ألا يُرى أن عَظْمَ الميت طاهر، فعَظم الحي أولى، فصار هذا باطناً ذلك الظاهر في مقابلته ، فسقط حكم الظاهر ؛ لعدمه، وعدم الحكم لعدم دليله لا يُعد من باب الخصوص على ما نبين في باب إبطال تخصيص العلل إن شاء الله تعالى.
ينعدم
وأما الذي ظهر فساده، واستترت صحته وأثره فهو القياس الذي عمل به الله ، قابله استحسان ظهر أثره، واستتر فساده، فسقط العمل به.
علماؤنا رحمهم
مثاله : أنهم قالوا فيمن تلا آية السجدة في الصلاة: أنه يركع بها قياساً؛
لأن النص قد ورد ،به قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَخَرَّ رَاكِعًا وَأَنَابَ ﴾ [ص: ٢٤]. وفي الاستحسان: لا يجوز؛ لأن الشرع أمرنا بالسجود، والركوع خلافه،
Chapter: Qiyas and Istihsan. Each one is of two types: As for one type of qiyas: that whose effect is weak. The second type: that whose corruption is apparent and whose soundness and effect are concealed. One type of istihsan: that whose effect is strong even if it is hidden. The second: that whose effect is apparent and whose corruption is hidden. Istihsan for us is one of the two qiyases, but it is called istihsan as an indication that it is the more preferable face to act upon, and acting upon the other is permissible, just as acting upon al-tard is permissible even though al-athar is more preferable. Istihsan has divisions: that which is established by athar (tradition), such as salam (sale with advance payment) and ijarah (lease) and the continuation of fasting despite the action of the forgetful person. And among it: that which is established by ijma (consensus), which is istisna (manufacturing contract). And among it: that which is established by necessity, which is purifying reservoirs, wells, and vessels. Our purpose here is only to classify the aspects of causes (ilal) with respect to rulings. Since for us the cause (illa) becomes a cause by its effect, we called that whose effect is weak: qiyas, and we called that whose effect is strong: istihsan, i.e., approved qiyas, and we gave precedence to the second, even though it is hidden, over the first, even though it is clear, because consideration is given to the strength of the effect, not to manifestation and clarity. Do you not see that the world is apparent and the Hereafter is hidden, yet the hidden is preferred due to strength, which is permanence, eternity, and purity, and the apparent is delayed due to the weakness of its effect – the heart and eyesight along with intellect? So the ruling of qiyas falls due to the opposition of the effect, just like [something] with istihsan due to its absence in estimation. Seven (?) Example of that: the leftover water of birds of prey in qiyas is najis (impure) because it is the leftover of something that is absolute, so it is like the leftover of predatory beasts, and this is the meaning of apparent effect because they are equal in the prohibition of eating. In istihsan it is pure (tahir) because the bird of prey is not intrinsically najis; evidence is the permissibility of benefiting from it legally, and its impurity has been established due to the prohibition of its meat, so we established a ruling between two rulings, which is adjacent impurity, so the attribute of impurity is established in its moisture and saliva. Birds of prey drink with the beak by way of taking then swallowing, and the bone is pure by itself, free from adjacency to impurity. Do you not see that the bone of a corpse is pure, so the bone of a living being is more so? So this became hidden in opposition to the apparent, so the ruling of the apparent fell due to its absence, and the absence of a ruling due to the absence of its evidence is not considered a case of specification (takhsis) as we will explain in the chapter on invalidation of specification of causes, God willing. As for that whose corruption is apparent and whose soundness and effect are concealed, it is the qiyas that God (?) worked with, facing it istihsan whose effect is apparent and its corruption is concealed, so acting upon it falls. Our scholars (may God have mercy on them) gave an example: they said regarding one who recites a verse of prostration in prayer: he bows for it by way of qiyas because the text has come regarding it. God Almighty said: {And he fell down bowing and repented} [Sad: 24]. In istihsan: it is not permissible because the law commanded us to prostrate, and bowing is contrary to that.
Source pages p. 612

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul is a key statement on the Hanafi classification of Qiyas and Istihsan. The author opens by stating each has two types. For Qiyas: one type has a weak effect (athar), meaning its legal consequence is weak; the other has apparent corruption but hidden soundness and effect—this type is invalid. For Istihsan: one type has a strong effect even if its rationale is hidden; the other has apparent effect but hidden corruption. The author then explains that in the Hanafi school, Istihsan is essentially one of the two types of Qiyas—specifically, the one that is preferred because its effect is stronger, even if the reasoning behind it is less obvious. Acting on the other (weaker) Qiyas remains permissible but is not preferred. The divisions of Istihsan are then listed: (1) established by transmitted tradition (athar), like salam and ijarah contracts, and the continuation of fasting despite a forgetful act; (2) established by consensus (ijma), like istisna (order for manufacture); (3) established by necessity, like purifying water sources. The central principle is that the strength of the effect (qūwat al-athar) is what determines precedence, not the clarity or obscurity of the reasoning. This is illustrated by the analogy of the world (apparent, weak) versus the Hereafter (hidden, strong). The example of the leftover water of birds of prey demonstrates this: by qiyas it would be impure (by analogy with predatory beasts), but by istihsan it is pure because the bird's beak and bone are clean, and the impurity is only adjacent and not intrinsic. The second example concerns reciting a verse of prostration in prayer: qiyas suggests bowing (based on the story of Prophet Dawud falling bowing), but istihsan rejects it because the legal command is to prostrate, not bow. Thus, the passage teaches how Hanafi usul prioritizes stronger effects and custom (istihsan) over strict analogy.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): A legal analogy where the 'illa (cause) is weak in effect, leading to a ruling that may be overridden by istihsan.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A method of juristic preference that gives precedence to a ruling with a stronger effect (athar) over a weaker qiyas, even if the weaker qiyas is more apparent.
الأثر (al-athar): The legal effect or consequence of a ruling; strength of athar determines the validity and precedence of a qiyas or istihsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazdawi, what determines whether a qiyas is set aside in favor of istihsan?
A) The clarity and appearance of the qiyas
B) The strength of the effect (athar) of the ruling
C) The consensus of the scholars on the qiyas
D) The absence of any textual proof

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, istihsan is a type of qiyas with a stronger effect; it does not invalidate weaker qiyas but is preferred.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
beginner
6 min
The Three Divisions of Istihsan
Enumeration of the three divisions of istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and give an example for each of the three divisions of istihsan: based on athar, ijma, and necessity.

Core Idea
Istihsan has three bases: tradition, consensus, and necessity.

After clarifying that istihsan is a preferred type of qiyas, al-Bazdawi enumerates the different ways istihsan can be established: by transmitted tradition (athar), by consensus (ijma), and by necessity. Each category has well-known fiqh examples that demonstrate how the strength of effect overrides the apparent analogy.

Guided Path
1
List the three divisions
Read the sentence: 'والاستحسان أقسام : وهو ما ثبت بالأثر، مثل السلم، والإجارة، وبقاء الصوم مع فعل الناسي. ومنه ما ثبت بالإجماع، وهو الاستصناع. ومنه ما ثبت بالضرورة، وهو تطهير الحياض والآبار والأواني.'
2
Memorize the examples
For each division, note the specific contract or ruling given: athar → salam, ijarah, continuation of fasting; ijma → istisna; necessity → purifying water sources.
3
Understand the legal reasoning
Each division shows a case where a qiyas might suggest a different ruling, but the established practice (athar), consensus, or necessity provides a stronger effect, thus istihsan is applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب
القياس والاستحسان
وكل واحد منهما على وجهين :
أما أحد نوعي القياس : فما ضعف أثره.
والنوع الثاني : ما ظهر فساده واستترت صحته وأثره.
وأحد نوعي الاستحسان: ما قوي أثره وإن كان خفياً.
والثاني : ما ظَهَرَ أثره، وخفي فساده.
وإنما الاستحسان عندنا أحد القياسين، لكنه استحساناً؛ إشارةً سمي إلى أنه الوجه الأولى في العمل به وأن العمل بالآخر جائز، كما جاز
العمل بالطرد وإن كان الأثر أولى منه.
والاستحسان أقسام : وهو ما ثبت بالأثر، مثل السلم، والإجارة،
وبقاء الصوم مع فعل الناسي.
ومنه ما ثبت بالإجماع، وهو الاستصناع.
ومنه ما ثبت بالضرورة ، وهو تطهير الحياض والآبار والأواني.
وإنما غرضنا ها هنا تقسيم وجوه العلل في حق الأحكام، ولما صارت العلة عندنا علةً بأثرها : سمينا الذي ضعف أثرها: قياساً، وسمينا الذي قَوِيَ أَثرها استحساناً، أي قياساً مُستحسناً، وقدمنا الثاني وإن كان خفياً
على الأول وإن كان جلياً ؛ لأن العبرة لقوة الأثر، دون الظهور والجلاء. ألا يُرى أن الدنيا ظاهرة، والعقبى باطنة، وقد ترجح الباطن لقوة ، وهو الدوام والخلود والصَّفوة، وتأخر الظاهر لضعف أثره، القلب، والبصر مع العقل، فسقط حكم القياس بمعارضة
الأثر،
و كالنفس مع الاستحسان؛ لعدمه في التقدير.
سبع
مثال ذلك : أن سؤر سباع الطير في القياس : نجس؛ لأنه سؤر ما هو مطلق، فكان كسور سباع البهائم، وهذا معنى ظاهر الأثر؛ لأنهما سواء في حرمة الأكل، وفي الاستحسان هو طاهر ؛ لأن السبع ليس بنجس العين؛ بدليل جواز الانتفاع به شرعاً، وقد ثبتت نجاسته ضرورة تحريم لحمه، فأثبتنا حكماً بین حكمين، وهو النجاسة المجاورة، فثبتت صفة النجاسة في رطوبته ولعابه، وسباعُ الطير تشرب بالمنقار على سبيل
الأخذ، ثم الابتلاع ، والعَظمُ طاهر بذاته، خال عن مجاورة النَّجَس. ألا يُرى أن عَظْمَ الميت طاهر، فعَظم الحي أولى، فصار هذا باطناً ذلك الظاهر في مقابلته ، فسقط حكم الظاهر ؛ لعدمه، وعدم الحكم لعدم دليله لا يُعد من باب الخصوص على ما نبين في باب إبطال تخصيص العلل إن شاء الله تعالى.

Key Terms
الأثر (al-athar): A transmitted tradition or established practice from the early Muslims that serves as proof for an istihsan ruling.
الإجماع (al-ijma): Consensus of the mujtahids, which is a source for istihsan.
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity that permits a departure from the strict ruling of qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Which of the following is NOT listed as a division of istihsan in this passage?
A) Established by athar
B) Established by ijma
C) Established by qiyas
D) Established by necessity

Key Takeaway
Istihsan is classified into three categories based on its proof: tradition, consensus, and necessity.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Precedence of Strong Athar: The Birds of Prey Case
Example illustrating how istihsan overrides qiyas based on strength of effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that strength of athar overrides apparent qiyas by analyzing the birds of prey example.

Core Idea
The leftover water of birds of prey is pure by istihsan despite apparent qiyas of impurity.

Al-Bazdawi provides a detailed example to illustrate how the strength of a legal effect (athar) can overturn a seemingly clear analogy. The case concerns the leftover water (su'ur) of birds of prey. By qiyas with land predators, it would be impure, but by istihsan it is pure because the effect of impurity is weak due to the bone being inherently pure. This demonstrates the principle that the hidden but strong effect takes precedence over the apparent but weak effect.

Guided Path
1
State the qiyas ruling
The qiyas: su'ur (leftover water) of birds of prey is impure (najis) by analogy with land predators, because both are prohibited to eat.
2
State the istihsan ruling
The istihsan ruling: it is pure (tahir) because birds of prey are not intrinsically impure; they are permitted to benefit from, and impurity is only established due to the prohibition of meat.
3
Identify the hidden strong effect
The hidden strong effect is that the bone of the bird is pure by itself, and it is free from direct contact with impurity. The beak does not carry impurity like the mouth of a land predator.
4
Apply the principle
The apparent qiyas (land predator analogy) has weak effect because the impurity is only adjacent, not intrinsic. The istihsan has stronger effect because it aligns with the original purity of the bone and the absence of direct impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And among it: that which is established by ijma (consensus), which is istisna (manufacturing contract). And among it: that which is established by necessity, which is purifying reservoirs, wells, and vessels. Our purpose here is only to classify the aspects of causes (ilal) with respect to rulings. Since for us the cause (illa) becomes a cause by its effect, we called that whose effect is weak: qiyas, and we called that whose effect is strong: istihsan, i.e., approved qiyas, and we gave precedence to the second, even though it is hidden, over the first, even though it is clear, because consideration is given to the strength of the effect, not to manifestation and clarity. Do you not see that the world is apparent and the Hereafter is hidden, yet the hidden is preferred due to strength, which is permanence, eternity, and purity, and the apparent is delayed due to the weakness of its effect – the heart and eyesight along with intellect? So the ruling of qiyas falls due to the opposition of the effect, just like [something] with istihsan due to its absence in estimation. Seven (?) Example of that: the leftover water of birds of prey in qiyas is najis (impure) because it is the leftover of something that is absolute, so it is like the leftover of predatory beasts, and this is the meaning of apparent effect because they are equal in the prohibition of eating. In istihsan it is pure (tahir) because the bird of prey is not intrinsically najis; evidence is the permissibility of benefiting from it legally, and its impurity has been established due to the prohibition of its meat, so we established a ruling between two rulings, which is adjacent impurity, so the attribute of impurity is established in its moisture and saliva. Birds of prey drink with the beak by way of taking then swallowing, and the bone is pure by itself, free from adjacency to impurity. Do you not see that the bone of a corpse is pure, so the bone of a living being is more so? So this became hidden in opposition to the apparent, so the ruling of the apparent fell due to its absence, and the absence of a ruling due to the absence of its evidence is not considered a case of specification (takhsis) as we will explain in the chapter on invalidation of specification of causes, God willing. As for that whose corruption is apparent and whose soundness and effect are concealed, it is the qiyas that God (?) worked with, facing it istihsan whose effect is apparent and its corruption is concealed, so acting upon it falls. Our scholars (may God have mercy on them) gave an example: they said regarding one who recites a verse of prostration in prayer: he bows for it by way of qiyas because the text has come regarding it. God Almighty said: {And he fell down bowing and repented} [Sad: 24]. In istihsan: it is not permissible because the law commanded us to prostrate, and bowing is contrary to that.
Source pages p. 612

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul is a key statement on the Hanafi classification of Qiyas and Istihsan. The author opens by stating each has two types. For Qiyas: one type has a weak effect (athar), meaning its legal consequence is weak; the other has apparent corruption but hidden soundness and effect—this type is invalid. For Istihsan: one type has a strong effect even if its rationale is hidden; the other has apparent effect but hidden corruption. The author then explains that in the Hanafi school, Istihsan is essentially one of the two types of Qiyas—specifically, the one that is preferred because its effect is stronger, even if the reasoning behind it is less obvious. Acting on the other (weaker) Qiyas remains permissible but is not preferred. The divisions of Istihsan are then listed: (1) established by transmitted tradition (athar), like salam and ijarah contracts, and the continuation of fasting despite a forgetful act; (2) established by consensus (ijma), like istisna (order for manufacture); (3) established by necessity, like purifying water sources. The central principle is that the strength of the effect (qūwat al-athar) is what determines precedence, not the clarity or obscurity of the reasoning. This is illustrated by the analogy of the world (apparent, weak) versus the Hereafter (hidden, strong). The example of the leftover water of birds of prey demonstrates this: by qiyas it would be impure (by analogy with predatory beasts), but by istihsan it is pure because the bird's beak and bone are clean, and the impurity is only adjacent and not intrinsic. The second example concerns reciting a verse of prostration in prayer: qiyas suggests bowing (based on the story of Prophet Dawud falling bowing), but istihsan rejects it because the legal command is to prostrate, not bow. Thus, the passage teaches how Hanafi usul prioritizes stronger effects and custom (istihsan) over strict analogy.

Key Terms
سؤر (su'ur): Leftover water after an animal drinks from it.
سباع الطير (siba' al-tayr): Birds of prey, such as hawks, eagles, falcons.
النجاسة المجاورة (al-najasah al-mujawirah): Adjacent impurity – impurity that is not intrinsic but arises from prohibition of consumption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the istihsan ruling for birds of prey's leftover water is considered stronger than the qiyas?
A) The bird's meat is not prohibited
B) The bird's beak is made of pure bone
C) The bird is a scavenger
D) The water is scarce

Key Takeaway
The birds of prey example shows that a hidden strong effect (pure bone) can override an apparent but weak qiyas (impurity by analogy).

Istihsan Overrides Apparent Qiyas: The Prostration Verse Case
Example where istihsan overrides qiyas using a Quranic verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why istihsan rejects the qiyas of bowing upon reciting a prostration verse, using the example from the Quran.

Core Idea
Qiyas suggests bowing, but istihsan commands prostration – effect over analogy.

Al-Bazdawi gives a second example, contrasting a clear qiyas with a stronger istihsan. When a person recites a verse of prostration (sajdah) in prayer, qiyas based on the story of Prophet Dawud (peace be upon him) might suggest bowing (ruku') instead of prostration. However, istihsan rejects this because the specific legal command is to prostrate, not bow. This demonstrates that the explicit text (amr) has a stronger effect than a weak analogy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the qiyas argument
The qiyas cites the verse from Surah Sad where Prophet Dawud 'fell down bowing' (kharra raki'an) as a precedent for bowing upon reciting a prostration verse.
2
Identify the istihsan response
Istihsan rules that bowing is not permissible; the required act is prostration (sajdah), as commanded by the law (shar').
3
Analyze why istihsan prevails
The qiyas is weak because the verse describes a specific event (Prophet Dawud's repentance) not a general command. The stronger effect is the explicit command to prostrate for tilawah (recitation of prostration verses).

القياس والاستحسان
وكل واحد منهما على وجهين :
أما أحد نوعي القياس : فما ضعف أثره.
والنوع الثاني : ما ظهر فساده واستترت صحته وأثره.
وأحد نوعي الاستحسان: ما قوي أثره وإن كان خفياً.
والثاني : ما ظَهَرَ أثره، وخفي فساده.
وإنما الاستحسان عندنا أحد القياسين، لكنه استحساناً؛ إشارةً سمي إلى أنه الوجه الأولى في العمل به وأن العمل بالآخر جائز، كما جاز
العمل بالطرد وإن كان الأثر أولى منه.

وبقاء الصوم مع فعل الناسي.
ومنه ما ثبت بالإجماع، وهو الاستصناع.
ومنه ما ثبت بالضرورة ، وهو تطهير الحياض والآبار والأواني.

الأثر،
و كالنفس مع الاستحسان؛ لعدمه في التقدير.

الأخذ، ثم الابتلاع ، والعَظمُ طاهر بذاته، خال عن مجاورة النَّجَس. ألا يُرى أن عَظْمَ الميت طاهر، فعَظم الحي أولى، فصار هذا باطناً ذلك الظاهر في مقابلته ، فسقط حكم الظاهر ؛ لعدمه، وعدم الحكم لعدم دليله لا يُعد من باب الخصوص على ما نبين في باب إبطال تخصيص العلل إن شاء الله تعالى.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Invalidity of Specifying Effective Causes (Takhsis al-'Ilal)
Debating the validity of specifying legal causes due to preventers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on takhsis al-'illah and apply al-Bazdawi's argument to reject an unsupported claim of specification.

Core Idea
Specification of a legal cause is invalid because it creates textual conflict akin to naskh or istithna'.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul tackles a critical debate: can a legal cause ('illah) be specified by a preventer (man')? Some Hanafi scholars argued yes, viewing it as mere explanation. Al-Bazdawi refutes this, establishing that causes cannot be specified like general texts, and any claim of specification must be supported by explicit evidence. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the Hanafi position
Recognize that the core question is whether a cause can be specified (makhsus) due to a preventer. The author (al-Bazdawi) holds that it is invalid.
2
Analyze the opposing argument
Some Hanafis argue that specification is not contradiction; it is like takhsis of general texts. They claim that when a cause exists without effect, it may be due to a preventer, not a defect in the cause.
This view is presented fairly before refutation.
3
Follow al-Bazdawi's response and the five-fold division
Al-Bazdawi counters that mere assertion of a preventer is insufficient; the preventer must be shown. He then categorizes preventers into five types: those preventing formation, perfection, ruling's beginning, ruling's completion, and ruling's bindingness.
Examples from archery and fiqh illustrate each type.
4
Grasp the final proof against specification
The author's key argument: evidence for specification resembles abrogation (naskh) or exception (istithna'), leading to textual conflict. This cannot be resolved like ordinary takhsis of 'amm.
Thus specification of causes is invalid.
5
Distinguish from takhsis of general texts
Understand that general texts (nusus) can be specified without corruption, but causes are derived attributes; specification implies inconsistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب فساد تخصيص العِلل
من أصحابنا من أجاز تخصيص العلل المؤثرة، وذلك بأن يقول: كانت علَّتي توجب ذلك، لكنه لم توجب لمانع، فصار مخصوصاً من العلة بهذا الدليل. واحتج بأن التخصيص غيرُ المناقضة لغةً، وهذا ظاهر؛ لأنه بيانُ أنه لم يدخل لا نقض ولا إبطال وقد صح الخصوص على الكتاب والسنة، دون المناقضة.
وقال : ولأن المعدول عن القياس بسنّة، أو إجماع، أو ضرورة، أو استحسان مخصوص منه بالإجماع.
ولأن الخصم ادعى أن هذا الوصف علة، فإذا وُجد ولا حكم له : احتمل أن يكون العدم لفساد العلة فيتناقض ويحتمل أن يكون العدمُ لمانع، فوجب أن يُقبل.
بيانه إن أبرز مانعاً وإلا فقد تناقض، ولذلك لا يُقبل مجرد قوله : خص بدليل؛ لاحتمال الفساد ، بخلاف النصوص؛ لأنها لا تحتمل فساداً.
وبني على هذا تقسيم الموانع، وهي خمسةٌ حاً وحكماً:
١ - مانع يمنع انعقاد العلة.
٢- ومانع يمنع تمام العلة. ٣- ومانع يمنع حكم العلة.
٤- ومانع يمنع تمام الحكم.
٥- ومانع يمنع لزوم الحكم.
وذلك في الرامي إذا انقطع وَتَرُه ، أو انكسر فوق سهمه، فلم ينعقد علة، وإذا حال بينه وبين مقصده حائط مَنَعَ تمامَ العلة حتى لم يصل إلى المحل. ومانع يمنع ابتداء الحكم، وهو أن يصيبه، فيدفعه بترس، أو غيره. والذي يمنع تمام الحكم أن يجرحه، ثم يداويه، فيندمل. والذي يمنع لزومه أن يصيبه فيمرض به ، ويصير صاحب فراش، ثم يصير له كطَبْع خامس، فيأمن منه غالباً، بمنزلة من ضربه الفالج، فيصير مفلوجاً كان مريضاً، فإن امتد، فصار طبعاً صار في حكم الصحيح. ومثاله من الشرعيات البيع إذا أضيف إلى حُرٌّ: لم ينعقد، وإذا أُضيف إلى مال غير مملوك للبائع : مَنَعَ تمام الانعقاد في حق المالك. وخيار الشرط يمنعُ ابتداءً الحكم، وخيار الرؤية يمنع تمام الحكم، وخيار العيب يمنع لزوم الحكم.
وأما الدليل على صحة ما ادعينا من إبطال خصوص العلل: أن تفسير الخصوص ما مر ذكره: أن دليل الخصوص يُشبه الناسخ بصيغته، ويُشبه الاستثناء بحكمه، وإذا كان كذلك : وقع التعارض بين النصين، فلم يفسد أحدهما بصاحبه، ولكن النص العام يلحقه ضرب من الاستعارة
Chapter: Invalidity of Specifying Causes. Some of our companions permitted the specification of effective causes, such that one says: my cause necessitated that, but it was not necessitated due to a preventer, so it became specified from the cause by this evidence. And he argued that specification is not contradiction linguistically, and this is apparent; because it is an explanation that neither nullification nor invalidation enters, and specification has been valid for the Book and Sunnah, without contradiction. And he said: And because what is deviated from analogy by a sunna, consensus, necessity, or istihsan is specified by consensus. And because the opponent claimed that this description is a cause; so when it exists but has no ruling, it is probable that the absence is due to invalidity of the cause, causing contradiction, and probable that the absence is due to a preventer, so it must be accepted. Its clarification: if he produces a preventer, otherwise he has contradicted himself; therefore his mere statement 'specified by evidence' is not accepted due to the possibility of invalidity, unlike texts because they do not admit invalidity. Based on this is the division of preventers, and they are five: sensorial and ruling: 1- A preventer that prevents the formation of the cause. 2- A preventer that prevents the perfection of the cause. 3- A preventer that prevents the ruling of the cause. 4- A preventer that prevents the perfection of the ruling. 5- A preventer that prevents the bindingness of the ruling. That is in the archer: if his bowstring breaks or the tip of his arrow breaks, the cause is not formed; and if a wall intervenes between him and his target, it prevents the perfection of the cause such that it does not reach the locus. And a preventer that prevents the beginning of the ruling: that it hits him but he deflects it with a shield or other. And that which prevents the perfection of the ruling: that he injures him, then treats him, so it heals. And that which prevents its bindingness: that it hits him and he falls ill due to it, becoming bedridden, then it becomes like a fifth nature, so he is generally safe from it, akin to one struck by paralysis becoming paralyzed while previously ill; if it continues and becomes a habit, he becomes in the ruling of a healthy person. And its example from the shari'ah: sale - if it is attributed to a free person, it is not formed; if attributed to property not owned by the seller, it prevents the perfection of formation regarding the owner. Option of stipulation prevents the beginning of the ruling, option of sight prevents the perfection of the ruling, option of defect prevents the bindingness of the ruling. As for the evidence for the validity of what we claim of invalidating the specification of causes: that the interpretation of specification is as previously mentioned: that the evidence of specification resembles the abrogator in form and resembles the exception in its ruling; and if so, a conflict occurs between the two texts, so neither invalidates the other, but the general text is subject to a kind of metaphorical interpretation.
Source pages p. 623

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul tackles the issue of whether a legal cause ('illah) can be specified (makhsus) when a preventer (man') arises. The author begins by reporting that some Hanafi scholars permit the specification of effective causes, arguing that specification does not entail logical contradiction (naqd) linguistically; rather, it is a clarification that the cause was not operative due to the preventer, just as general texts of the Quran and Sunnah are specified without contradiction. They further argue that deviation from analogy (qiyas) due to a specific text, consensus, necessity, or istihsan is itself a form of specification by consensus, and that when a claimed cause exists but yields no ruling, the absence could be due either to a defect in the cause (contradiction) or to a preventer — and the latter possibility should be accepted. However, the author dismisses this: if the preventer is not explicitly shown, the claim is contradictory; mere assertion of specification is not accepted because of the possibility of the cause's corruption, unlike original texts (nusus) which cannot be corrupt. The author then builds on the necessity of preventers to divide them into five categories: (1) preventer of the formation of the cause (e.g., archer's broken string prevents the cause of shooting from existing), (2) preventer of the perfection of the cause (e.g., a wall blocking the arrow's path), (3) preventer of the ruling's beginning (e.g., arrow deflected by shield), (4) preventer of the ruling's completion (e.g., wound heals after treatment), (5) preventer of the ruling's bindingness (e.g., the victim becomes chronically ill so the harm becomes habitual, like a paralysis that becomes normal). Analogous examples from fiqh: a sale attributed to a free person (who cannot be owned) prevents formation; attached to unowned property prevents formation's perfection regarding the owner; option of stipulation prevents the effect's beginning; option of sight prevents its perfection; option of defect prevents its bindingness. Finally, the author provides the definitive proof against the validity of specification of causes: the evidence for specification either resembles an abrogator (nasikh) in form or an exception (istithna') in ruling — either way, it creates a conflict of two texts which neither invalidates the other; instead, the general text undergoes metaphorical interpretation (isti'arah). Thus specification of a cause is invalid because it would imply textual conflict that cannot be resolved like ordinary takhsis of 'amm.

Key Terms
العلة (al-'illah): The effective legal cause that necessitates a ruling in qiyas.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): Specification of a general term or cause by a particular evidence, limiting its application.
المانع (al-man'): A preventer that blocks the operation of a cause, its ruling, or its effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazdawi, why is the specification of a cause (takhsis al-'illah) invalid?
A) Because causes are always clear and need no specification.
B) Because specification of a cause resembles naskh or istithna', creating conflict between two texts.
C) Because preventers cannot exist for causes.
D) Because the opponent's argument is weak.

Key Takeaway
Specification of a legal cause ('illah) is invalid because it creates a conflict between texts, unlike specification of general texts.

Types of Preventers and the Hanafi Rejection of Cause Particularization
Analysis of preventers and refutation of cause particularization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the five types of preventers (mawāni‘) in Hanafi causality, explain the Hanafi rejection of particularization of causes (khuṣūṣ al-‘ilal), and apply this distinction to examples from qiyās and istihsān.

Core Idea
A preventer (māni‘) does not allow the cause to remain while blocking its effect; it negates the cause itself.

In Hanafi legal theory, causal reasoning (ta‘līl) is central to qiyās, but its operation is governed by the presence of a complete cause (‘illah). When a ruling is absent despite the apparent presence of a cause, scholars debate whether the absence is due to a preventer that temporarily blocks the effect while preserving the cause, or because the cause itself is incomplete. This passage sharply distinguishes five types of preventers and argues that any preventer actually removes the cause, not merely its effect. Based on this, the Hanafis reject the concept of particularization of causes (khuṣūṣ al-‘ilal) as advanced by some mutakallimūn, demonstrating that what appears to be a prevention is always a negation of the cause. Understanding this difference is essential for correctly applying qiyās and istihsān.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the five preventers from the archer analogy
The text begins with a physical analogy of an archer to illustrate how a preventer can intervene at different stages. Identify each preventer and which stage of the causal process it affects: (1) prevents the cause from being established (broken bowstring/arrow), (2) prevents completion of the cause (wall intervening), (3) prevents initiation of the ruling (shield deflects), (4) prevents completion of the ruling (wound heals), (5) prevents the ruling from becoming binding (illness becomes chronic).
The archer analogy is a clear mental model for the multi-stage causality in legal reasoning.
2
Map the preventers to legal examples
The passage provides legal counterparts for each preventer using contracts and options. Match each stage with its shar‘ī example: (1) sale with a free person (cause not established), (2) sale of another's property (incomplete conclusion), (3) khiyār al-shart (prevents initiation), (4) khiyār al-ru’ya (prevents completion), (5) khiyār al-‘ayb (prevents binding).
These examples show the preventers in action in familiar fiqh contexts.
3
Understand the opposing theory of khuṣūṣ al-‘ilal
Some scholars argue that when a cause (e.g., a general 'illah) meets a preventer, the cause remains operative but its ruling is temporarily blocked for that specific instance, analogizing it to the specification of a general text (takhṣīṣ al-‘āmm). The text labels this as 'particularization of causes' (khuṣūṣ al-‘ilal).
This view treats a preventer like a specific evidence that restricts the cause's scope, not invalidates it.
4
Analyse the Hanafi proof against particularization
The author provides a rational proof: if particularization were allowed in causes, it would lead to validating every mujtahid and imply that ijtihād is infallible, which is impossible. In reality, absence of ruling is due to increase or decrease in the description (waṣf) of the cause; that change makes the cause cease to exist. Therefore, the absence should be attributed to 'absence of cause', not to a preventer that maintains the cause.
Key distinction: the cause is defined by its conditions; a change means it is no longer the same cause.
5
Apply the Hanafi position to cases of conflict with text, consensus, or istihsān
When a cause conflicts with a direct text, consensus, or istihsān, the Hanafis hold that the cause becomes void (not merely particularized). The ruling's absence is due to the cause's non-existence. This is the basis of istihsān: the qiyās is abandoned not because it is overridden by a particularizer but because the cause itself is not effective in that context.
This aligns with the overall Hanafi approach that causes are not subject to specification like texts.

And a preventer prevents the completion of the cause. And a preventer prevents the ruling of the cause. And a preventer prevents the completion of the ruling. And a preventer prevents the binding of the ruling. That is in the example of the archer: if his bowstring breaks or the head of his arrow snaps, the cause is not established; and if a wall intervenes between him and his target, it prevents the completion of the cause so that it does not reach the locus. And a preventer prevents the initiation of the ruling: that he strikes [the target] but [the target] deflects it with a shield or similar. And that which prevents the completion of the ruling: that he wounds [the target], then treats it, and it heals. And that which prevents its binding: that it hits him, he becomes ill, becomes bedridden, then it becomes like a fifth nature, so he is generally safe from it, like one struck by paralysis who becomes paralyzed after being ill; if it persists and becomes a habit, he becomes in the ruling of the healthy. Its example from legal rulings: sale if attached to a free person: it is not concluded; if attached to property not owned by the seller: it prevents complete conclusion in the right of the owner. The option of stipulation prevents the initiation of the ruling, the option of sight prevents the completion of the ruling, and the option of defect prevents the binding of the ruling. As for the proof of the validity of our claim in invalidating particularization of causes: that the interpretation of particularization has been mentioned previously: that the evidence of particularization resembles the abrogator in its form and resembles the exception in its effect, and when it is so, conflict occurs between the two texts, and neither invalidates the other, but the general text undergoes a kind of metaphorical usage, in that part of it is intended while it remains authoritative, as previously. This never occurs in causes because that leads to validating every mujtahid and necessitates infallibility of ijtihad from error and contradiction, and that involves a doctrine of the best. But the ruling is only prevented by an increase or decrease of a description, which we call a particularizing preventer, and by its increase or decrease the cause changes, so absence must be attributed to absence of cause, not to a preventer that necessitates particularization while the cause exists. The difference between us and them regarding effective causes is that they attribute absence of ruling despite the existence of cause to a preventer that necessitates particularization while the cause exists, making it like an evidence of particularization in part of what the general text covers despite the existence of general evidence, while we attribute absence to absence of cause because the cause ceases to exist by the absence of its description or its increase, and absence due to absence is not a matter of particularization. This is the way of our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) in istihsan, because if analogy is abandoned due to a text, then the ruling of the cause is absent because of its absence; for the cause is not made a cause in opposition to the text, so its ruling becomes void due to its absence, not while it exists by a particularizing evidence. Unlike the case of two texts, because one does not invalidate the other, so particularization must be asserted. Likewise, if [the cause] is opposed by consensus or necessity: the description does not remain a cause, because necessity is also a consensus, and consensus is like the Book and Sunnah. As for if it is opposed by istihsan: it necessitates the absence of the former due to what we mentioned in the chapter of istihsan, so absence of ruling is due to absence of cause, so it is not a case of particularization. And similarly we say regarding all effective causes.
Source pages p. 624

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the concept of manis (preventers) in causality and a refutation of the theory of particularization of causes (خصوص العلل) attributed to some scholars, likely the Mutakallimin or Shafi‘is. The text first enumerates five types of manis: (1) prevents the cause from being established (e.g., broken bowstring), (2) prevents the completion of the cause (e.g., a wall blocking the arrow), (3) prevents the initiation of the ruling (e.g., target deflects with a shield), (4) prevents the completion of the ruling (e.g., wound heals), and (5) prevents the ruling from becoming binding (e.g., illness becomes chronic so the effect is no longer expected). Legal examples are given: sale with a free person (not a proper subject), sale of another's property, and the options (khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'ya, khiyar al-'ayb) which affect different stages. The author then argues against the concept of particularization of causes: they reason that if one could attribute absence of ruling to a manis while the cause is still complete, this would be analogous to particularization of a general text by a specific evidence. However, the Hanafi position is that the cause itself is absent when its conditions are not fully met; the manis in reality indicates the absence of the cause, not a separate particularizer. Accepting particularization would lead to the unacceptable consequence of validating every mujtahid's opinion and imply infallibility. The Hanafis attribute absence of ruling to absence of cause, not to a manis that particularizes. This difference has practical effects in cases where a cause is opposed by text, consensus, necessity, or istihsan. The Hanafis hold that the cause is voided in such opposition, so the ruling's absence is due to lack of cause, not a particularizing preventer. The text explicitly states that this is the method of the Hanafi scholars (أصحابنا) in istihsan.

Key Terms
المانع (al-māni‘): What prevents the effect of the cause or the ruling from occurring, without necessarily negating the cause entirely according to some schools, but Hanafis hold it negates the cause by altering its description.
خصوص العلل (khuṣūṣ al-‘ilal): The theory that a cause can be restricted in its application by a preventer, similar to how a general text is specified by a particular evidence.
تمام العلة (tamām al-‘illah): The cause reaching its full stage where it is ready to produce its ruling.
لزوم الحكم (luzūm al-ḥukm): The binding nature of the ruling, meaning it becomes obligatory or final.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the Hanafi view on the absence of a ruling when a cause meets a preventer?
A) The cause remains complete but its ruling is not applied in this particular case due to a specific preventer.
B) The preventer eliminates the cause entirely, so the absence of ruling is due to the absence of the cause.
C) The cause is abrogated by the preventer.
D) The preventer only affects the ruling, not the cause.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a preventer (māni‘) negates the cause by changing its description, so the absence of a ruling is always due to absence of cause, never to particularization of the cause.

Hanafi Response to Takhsis in Effective Causes
Dispute on takhsis in effective causes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi position that absence of ruling is due to absence of ‘illah from the opposing view that it is due to a preventer (mani‘), and apply this distinction to the examples of fasting and ghasb.

Core Idea
Absence of ruling is absence of cause itself – never specification of an operative cause.

This passage presents a fundamental dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: when a ruling does not apply even though the cause (‘illah) appears to be present, is that because the cause has been specified (takhsis) by a preventer, or because the cause itself is absent? The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, insists on the latter: the cause changes with its descriptors, so its absence is not a form of takhsis. This distinction underlies the Hanafi theory of istihsan and has profound implications for legal reasoning. Understanding this principle is key to mastering how Hanafis reconcile apparent contradictions between qiyas and other sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Read the opening lines to understand the central issue: when a ruling is absent despite the apparent presence of the ‘illah, do we attribute it to a preventer that specifies the ‘illah (the opposing view) or to the absence of the ‘illah itself (the Hanafi view)?
The opponents are likely the Shafi‘i school or the Mutakallimun.
2
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
Focus on the Hanafi argument: the ‘illah is defined by a precise set of descriptors; increase or decrease in these descriptors changes the ‘illah. Therefore, when a ruling is absent, it is because the ‘illah is no longer the same. This is not takhsis but ‘adam al-‘illah.
The author emphasizes that attributing absence to a preventer would lead to taswib (validating all ijtihad) and is logically unsound.
3
Contrast with the opposing view
The opponents say the ruling is absent because a preventer (mani‘) specifies the application of the ‘illah, even though the ‘illah itself remains. This is analogous to takhsis of a general text by a specific evidence.
The Hanafis reject this because it treats rational causes like linguistic formulations.
4
Analyze the examples
Examine the two examples: (1) the forgetful person who pours water into his throat while fasting – Hanafis say the fast is valid because the ‘illah (loss of pillar) is absent; opponents say a preventer (pardon) specifies the ‘illah. (2) Ghasb of a mudabbar slave – Hanafis say the ‘illah of ownership of substitute is absent because the guarantee is not for the property itself; opponents say a preventer (the slave not being transferable) specifies the ‘illah.
The author concludes that the Hanafi interpretation is correct, as it preserves the consistency of the ‘illah.
5
Apply the principle to coextensive causes
Note the concession: specification (takhsis) can apply to coextensive causes (al-‘ilal al-tardiyyah), which are defined by wording rather than meaning. This is because expressions, not pure meanings, are amenable to specification.
This distinction reinforces that effective causes, being based on rational meanings, are not subject to takhsis.

And like our saying regarding ghasb (usurpation): that when it became a cause for ownership of substitute property, it should be a cause for ownership of the substituted. As for the mudabbar (slave whose manumission is deferred): the ruling of this cause is prevented due to a preventer, which is that the usurped property does not admit of transfer, so this would be specification, and this is false. Rather, the correct is what we said: the ruling is absent due to the absence of the cause, which is that ghasb is a cause for ownership of the substitute of the usurped property; because the guarantee of the mudabbar is not a substitute for the usurped property, but rather a substitute for the lost hand; because we said it is not a locus for transfer. So what they made as evidence of specification, we made it evidence of absence, and this is the foundation of this section, so preserve it and master it, for in it is much fiqh and great deliverance. And specification only applies to coextensive causes (al-‘ilal al-tardiyyah); because they are based on their wording. And specification applies to expressions, not pure meanings. And from that: our saying regarding zina that it necessitates the prohibition of affinity; because it is a tillage for the child, so it is made in its place, and since the child is created from their water, or they unite upon intercourse
Source pages p. 625

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (khilaf) between the Hanafis and other schools (likely the Shafi'is or Mutakallimun) regarding the treatment of effective causes (al-‘ilal al-mu’aththira) when a ruling is absent despite the apparent presence of the ‘illah. The opponents attribute the absence to a preventer (mani‘) that necessitates specification (takhsis) — i.e., the ‘illah is still operative but a specific condition prevents its effect in that case. The Hanafis, led by Abu Hanifa and his students, attribute the absence to the absence of the ‘illah itself, because the ‘illah is defined by a precise set of descriptors (awsaf); if any of these descriptors is missing or an extra descriptor is present, the ‘illah is no longer the same and thus the ruling does not apply. This is not takhsis but rather a change in the ‘illah. The author explains that this Hanafi approach is the basis of istihsan: when qiyas is abandoned due to a text, consensus, necessity, or istihsan, it is because the ‘illah has ceased to exist, not because the ‘illah is overridden by a mukhassis. Two examples illustrate the point: (1) Fasting: The ‘illah for invalidation of fast is the loss of the pillar (rkn) — i.e., allowing water to reach the throat. For a forgetful person, the same physical act occurs but the ruling is different; the opponents say there is a preventer (the effect of forgetfulness being pardoned), while the Hanafis say the ‘illah is absent because the forgetful person's act is attributed to the Lawgiver and thus the element of transgression is missing, so the pillar of fasting remains intact. (2) Ghasb (usurpation): The ‘illah for ownership of substitute is that ghash is a cause for ownership of the substitute property. For a mudabbar slave (whose manumission is conditional upon the master's death), the opponent says the ruling is prevented because the mudabbar is not subject to transfer — a specification. The Hanafis say the ruling is absent because the guarantee here is not a substitute for the usurped property but for the lost hand (i.e., the hand that wrongfully took the slave), so the ‘illah of being a substitute for the property itself is not present. The author concludes that specification only applies to coextensive causes (al-‘ilal al-tardiyyah) that are based on wording, not to pure meanings. The passage emphasizes that this principle is key to much fiqh and provides a solution to many legal problems.

Key Terms
العلة المؤثرة (al-‘illah al-mu’aththirah): A cause that is effective in producing a ruling, defined by a set of descriptors; its presence or absence determines the ruling.
المانع المخصص (al-māni‘ al-mukhassis): A preventer that specifies the application of a general cause, opposite to the Hanafi view.
العلل الطردية (al-‘ilal al-tardiyyah): Coextensive causes that are defined purely by wording (lafz) rather than by meaning; specification can apply to them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, when the ruling is absent despite the apparent presence of the 'illah, what is the reason?
A) The ruling is absent due to a preventer that specifies the 'illah.
B) The ruling is absent because the 'illah is no longer present due to a change in its descriptors.
C) The ruling is absent because the 'illah is overridden by a stronger text.
D) The ruling is absent due to consensus or necessity that nullifies the 'illah.

Key Takeaway
The absence of a ruling in a case is due to the absence of the effective cause ('illah), not to a specifying preventer.

The Forgetful Fasting Person: Absence of 'Illah vs Takhsis
Defense of Hanafi position on absence of 'illah using the fasting example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that when a qiyas ruling does not apply to a specific case, it is due to the absence of the 'illah (legal cause) rather than specification of the 'illah, using the example of the forgetful fasting person.

Core Idea
A forgetful person's fast is valid because the 'illah of transgression is absent, not because the 'illah is specified.

In this lesson, we examine a key dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: when a ruling derived by qiyas does not apply to a particular case, is it because the legal cause is specified (takhsis) or because the cause is absent? The Hanafi school emphatically defends the latter position. We begin with the classic example of the fasting person who forgetfully swallows water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling and its 'illah
Recall the ruling: deliberately pouring water into one's mouth invalidates the fast. The 'illah is that the pillar (rkn) of fasting—intentional restraint—is lost. Then consider the forgetful person: the ruling does not apply. The question is why.
2
Examine the opposing argument (takhsis)
Those who allow takhsis of the 'illah argue that the 'illah (loss of pillar) is still present, but a preventer (mani')—the Quranic pardon for forgetfulness—blocks its effect. Thus the 'illah is specified, i.e., it applies generally except where a text removes it.
This is like saying 'the cause exists but is prevented'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi argues that the act of the forgetful person is attributed to the Lawgiver (since the Lawgiver waives punishment), so the meaning of transgression (jinaayah) is absent. Hence the 'illah itself—intentional transgression—is not present. The fast remains because its pillar survives; it's not that the 'illah is prevented but that the 'illah does not exist.
The Hanafi denies that there is a preventer; rather, the cause is missing.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference matters in other cases: if specification were allowed, one would need a textual preventer for every exception. If the 'illah is absent, one can simply deny the 'illah in any case where the ruling does not apply, without needing a separate textual basis. This affects the structure of qiyas and the burden of proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبيان ذلك: في قولنا في الصائم إذا صُب الماء في حلقه : إنه يفسد صومه ؛ لأن ركن الصوم قد فات. ويلزم عليه الناسي، فمَن أجاز الخصوص قال: امتنع حكم هذا التعليل ثمة؛ لمانع، وهو الأثر. وقلنا نحن امتنع لعدم هذه العلة؛ لأن فعل الناسي منسوب إلى صاحب الشرع ، فسقط عنه معنى الجناية، وصار الفعل عفوا، فبقي الصوم لبقاء ركنه لا لمانع مع فوات ركنه. ومثل قولنا في الغصب : إنه لما صار سبباً لملك بدل المال: وجب أن يكون سبباً لملك المبدل. وأما المدبَّر : فإنما امتنع حكم هذه العلة فيه لمانع ، وهو أن المغصوب لا يحتمل الانتقال فكان هذا تخصيصاً، وهذا باطل. وإنما الصحيح ما قلنا إن الحكم عُدم لعدم العلة، وهو كون الغصب سبباً لملك بدل العين المغصوبة ؛ لأن ضمان المدبّر ليس ببدل عن العين المغصوبة، لكنه بدل عن اليد الفائتة ؛ لما قلنا إنه ليس بمحل للنقل، فالذي جعل عندهم دليل الخصوص: جعلناه دليل العدم، وهذا أصلُ هذا الفصل، فاحفظه وأحكمه، ففيه فقه كثير ، ومَخلَص كبير. و* وإنما يلزم الخصوص على العلل الطردية؛ لأنها قائمة بصيغتها ور والخصوص يَرِدُّ على العبارات، دون المعاني الخالصة. 6 ومن ذلك : قولنا في الزنا إنه يوجب حرمة المصاهرة؛ لأنه حرث للولد، فأُقيم مقامه ، ولما خلق الولد من مائهما، أو اجتمعا على الوطء، وجاءت بينهما شبهة البعضية بواسطة الولد صارت بناتها وأمهاتها كبناته وأمهاته، وآباؤه وأبناؤه كآبائها وأبنائها فلزم على هذا أنه لم تَحرُم الأخوات والعمات والخالات، فقال أهلُ المقالة الأولى إنه مخصوص بالنص، مع قيام العلة. وقلنا : بل العلل صارت عللاً شرعاً، لا بذواتها، وهي لم تُجعل علةً عند معارضة النص، وفي هذا معارضةٌ؛ لأن حكم النص يزداد بامتداد الحرمة إلى الأخوات وغيرهن فلا تبقى علة عند معارضة النص، فيكون عدم الحكم : لعدم العلة. وليس هذا من باب الخصوص في شيء، وهذا واضح جداً. ومن أحكم المعرفة ، وأحسن الطويَّةَ سَهُلَ عليه تخريج الجُمَل على هذا الأصل إن شاء الله تعالى.
And its explanation: in our statement regarding the fasting person when water is poured into his throat: it invalidates his fast because the pillar of fasting has been lost. And it applies to the forgetful person. So whoever allowed specification said: the ruling of this cause is prevented there due to a preventer, which is the trace. And we said: it is prevented due to the absence of this cause, because the act of the forgetful is attributed to the Lawgiver, so the meaning of transgression falls away from him, and the act becomes pardoned, so the fast remains due to the survival of its pillar, not due to a preventer with the loss of its pillar. And similarly our statement regarding usurpation: when it became a cause for ownership of the replacement of property, it must be a cause for ownership of the original. As for the mudabbar slave, the ruling of this cause is prevented in his case due to a preventer, which is that the usurped item does not permit transfer; so this would be specification, and this is false. Rather the correct view is what we said: the ruling is absent due to the absence of the cause, which is that usurpation is a cause for ownership of the replacement of the usurped item, because the guarantee of the mudabbar is not a replacement for the usurped item, but a replacement for the lost possession; because we said it is not a locus for transfer. So what they made a proof of specification, we made a proof of absence. And this is the foundation of this chapter, so memorize it and master it, for in it is much jurisprudence and great deliverance. And specification only applies to formal causes because they are based on their wording, and specification applies to expressions, not to pure meanings. And from that is our statement regarding adultery: it necessitates the prohibition of marriage relations because it is a field for the child, so it stood in its place, and when the child is created from their fluids, or they come together in intercourse, and between them comes a semblance of partiality through the child, her daughters and mothers become like his daughters and mothers, and his fathers and sons become like her fathers and sons. So it follows from this that sisters, aunts, and maternal aunts are not prohibited. Then the proponents of the first opinion said: it is specified by the text, while the cause is valid. And we said: rather, causes become legal causes by revelation, not by themselves, and they are not made causes when they oppose the text. And in this is opposition, because the ruling of the text increases by the extension of prohibition to sisters and others, so the cause does not remain when opposing the text. Thus the absence of ruling is due to absence of cause. And this is not from the category of specification at all, and this is very clear. And whoever masters knowledge and has good intention, it will be easy for him to derive general rulings upon this principle, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 626

Commentary
This passage is a sustained usul dispute defending the Hanafi position that when a ruling derived from an 'illah (legal cause) is absent in a particular case, it is not due to a preventer (mani') that would specify the 'illah (takhsis), but rather due to the absence of the 'illah itself. The author begins with the example of a fasting person—if water is poured into his throat, the fast is invalidated because the pillar (rkn, namely restraint) is lost. However, for a forgetful person who unintentionally swallows water, the fast remains valid. Opponents (ahl al-takhsis) argue that the 'illah (losing the pillar) still exists but is prevented by a trace (athar, i.e., Quranic evidence pardoning forgetfulness). The Hanafis respond that the act of a forgetful person is attributed to the Lawgiver (since the Lawgiver waives punishment), so the act becomes pardoned ('afwan), meaning the 'illah of transgression is absent. Thus the fast remains because its pillar persists—not due to a preventer but because the 'illah is not present. Next, the author discusses ghasb (usurpation). The principle is that usurpation causes ownership of a replacement (badal mal). For a mudabbar slave (one promised freedom after master's death), opponents claim that if a mudabbar is usurped, the guarantee is not ownership of the slave himself (since he cannot be transferred) but compensation for lost possession. They say this specifies the 'illah: usurpation causes ownership of replacement except for non-transferable property. The Hanafis argue that the ruling is absent because the 'illah is different: for the mudabbar, the guarantee is not a replacement for the property but for the lost hand (i.e., possession), so the 'illah of causing ownership of replacement is not present at all. Thus, what opponents considered a proof of specification is actually a proof of absence of 'illah. The author then notes that specification only occurs in formal causes ('ilal tirdiyya) that are based on wording, not in causes based on pure meanings. Finally, the example of zina (adultery) is given: it creates an impediment to marriage (hurmah al-musaharah) because it is a cause for the child. The 'illah is that through the child, a semblance of partiality exists, so the adulterer's daughters and mothers become like his own. However, sisters, aunts, etc., are not prohibited by consensus. Opponents say the 'illah is still valid but is specified by text (i.e., the general rule is narrowed). Hanafis respond that causes are legal ('illa shar'iyya) not by themselves but by being made so by the Lawgiver. When a text explicitly limits the ruling (e.g., prohibiting only specific relatives), the 'illah cannot operate beyond the text's scope; hence the 'illah is not present for the excluded categories. Thus absence of ruling is again due to absence of 'illah, not specification. The author concludes that whoever understands this principle can easily derive rulings from it.

Key Terms
العلة (al-'illah): The legal cause ('illah) that grounds a ruling via qiyas; it is a Shar'i cause, not a real cause, and its existence is determined by the Lawgiver.
الخصوص / التخصيص (al-khusus / al-takhsis): Specification of an 'illah: the claim that a preventer prevents the 'illah from operating in a specific case while the 'illah itself remains valid.
المانع (al-mani'): A preventer that blocks the effect of the 'illah while the 'illah is present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this lesson, why is the forgetful person's fast valid?
A) Because the 'illah of losing the pillar is specified by the text.
B) Because the 'illah of transgression is absent since the act is pardoned.
C) Because a preventer blocks the effect of the 'illah.
D) Because the pillar of fasting was never lost.

Key Takeaway
When a qiyas ruling does not apply, the Hanafi school attributes it to absence of the 'illah rather than its specification, preserving the consistency of qiyas.

The Mudabbar Slave: Ruling Absent Due to Absence of 'Illah in Usurpation
Defense of Hanafi position on absence of 'illah using the mudabbar example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a ruling is absent due to absence of the 'illah by analyzing the case of the usurped mudabbar slave.

Core Idea
The mudabbar slave's guarantee is for possession, not ownership, so the 'illah for owning the original is absent.

This lesson continues the Hanafi defense of the 'absence of 'illah' principle using the example of usurpation (ghasb). The general rule is that usurpation makes one liable to replace the property with an equivalent. For a mudabbar slave (who is promised freedom after the master's death), the opponent claims that the rule is specified because the slave cannot be owned. The Hanafi responds that the 'illah is different: the guarantee is for the loss of possession, not for the property itself, so the 'illah for owning a replacement is absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule of ghasb
Recall the ruling: usurpation (ghasb) makes the usurper liable to own the replacement (badal) of the property taken. That is, if someone usurps property, they must either return it or pay its material replacement.
2
Apply to the mudabbar slave
A mudabbar slave is a slave whose master has promised freedom upon his death. If a mudabbar is usurped, the ruling is that the usurper does not own the slave (since the slave cannot be transferred) but instead guarantees the loss of possession (al-yad). The opponent says this shows the rule is specified: the 'illah (ownership of replacement) is blocked by a preventer (the slave's non-transferability).
3
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi argues that the guarantee for the mudabbar is not a replacement for the property (the slave) but a replacement for the lost possession (yad fa'ita). Thus the 'illah—that usurpation causes ownership of the replacement of the property—is not present at all. The 'illah was that ghasb leads to ownership of the replacement of the specific item; here, the item cannot be owned, so the 'illah is different.
4
Understand the broader principle
What the opponent took as evidence of specification (the non-transferability) is actually evidence of absence of the 'illah. This is the foundation of the chapter: in all such cases, we check whether the same 'illah exists; if it does not, the ruling does not apply, without invoking specification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Opponents say the 'illah is still valid but is specified by text (i.e., the general rule is narrowed). Hanafis respond that causes are legal ('illa shar'iyya) not by themselves but by being made so by the Lawgiver. When a text explicitly limits the ruling (e.g., prohibiting only specific relatives), the 'illah cannot operate beyond the text's scope; hence the 'illah is not present for the excluded categories. Thus absence of ruling is again due to absence of 'illah, not specification. The author concludes that whoever understands this principle can easily derive rulings from it.

Key Terms
المدبر (al-mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom after the master's death; during the master's life, the slave is still owned but is not transferable by sale.
الغصب (al-ghasb): Usurpation; taking someone's property without right.
بدل اليد (badal al-yad): Compensation for the loss of possession, not for the property itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, why does the mudabbar slave not fall under the general rule of replacing usurped property?
A) Because the 'illah is specified due to the slave's non-transferability.
B) Because the 'illah for owning a replacement is absent; the guarantee is for possession.
C) Because the general rule does not apply to slaves at all.
D) Because the mudabbar can be returned, so no replacement is needed.

Key Takeaway
In cases where the nature of the liability differs, the Hanafi sees absence of 'illah rather than specification.
