Zina and Prohibition of Marriage: 'Illah Limited by Text, Not Specified
Defense of Hanafi position using the example of zina and marriage prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position that the 'illah for prohibition of marriage in zina does not extend to relatives not mentioned in the text, due to absence of the 'illah rather than its specification.

Core Idea
Legal causes are defined by the Lawgiver; when a text limits a prohibition, the 'illah does not exist beyond that limit.

This lesson presents the third example in the author's defense: the prohibition of marriage due to zina (adultery). The general ruling is that zina creates a prohibition of marriage between the adulterer and the relatives of the adulterous partner (e.g., the adulterer cannot marry the partner's mother or daughter). However, the prohibition does not extend to the partner's sisters, aunts, etc. The opponent says the 'illah (the creation of a semblance of partiality through the child) is present but specified by the text. The Hanafi argues that the 'illah is only effective as defined by the Lawgiver; the text explicitly limits the prohibition, so the 'illah does not exist for excluded relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the 'illah for marriage prohibition in zina
The 'illah is that zina creates a semblance of partiality (shubhat al-ba'diyyah) through the child, making the partner's mothers and daughters like one's own. Therefore, those relatives are prohibited.
2
Note which relatives are not prohibited
Sisters, aunts, and maternal aunts are not prohibited by consensus. The question is why: is it because the 'illah is specified (i.e., the cause exists but is narrowed by text), or because the 'illah does not extend to them?
3
Examine the opposing view
The opponents (ahl al-mad'dat al-ula) say the 'illah is valid but is specified by the text that enumerates prohibited relatives. So the 'illah is general but limited by textual exception.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi says causes are legal (shar'iyya) by nature; they are not independent realities. When a text explicitly contradicts a potential extension, the 'illah is not made by the Lawgiver for that case. The 'illah for prohibition is thus absent for sisters and aunts because the Lawgiver did not include them. The ruling of prohibition is based on the text, and the 'illah does not operate beyond it. The author also notes that specification (takhsis) only applies to formal causes based on wording ('ilal tirdiyya), not to causes based on pure meanings. The 'illah in zina is meaning-based, so takhsis cannot apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبيان ذلك: في قولنا في الصائم إذا صُب الماء في حلقه : إنه يفسد صومه ؛ لأن ركن الصوم قد فات. ويلزم عليه الناسي، فمَن أجاز الخصوص قال: امتنع حكم هذا التعليل ثمة؛ لمانع، وهو الأثر. وقلنا نحن امتنع لعدم هذه العلة؛ لأن فعل الناسي منسوب إلى صاحب الشرع ، فسقط عنه معنى الجناية، وصار الفعل عفوا، فبقي الصوم لبقاء ركنه لا لمانع مع فوات ركنه. ومثل قولنا في الغصب : إنه لما صار سبباً لملك بدل المال: وجب أن يكون سبباً لملك المبدل. وأما المدبَّر : فإنما امتنع حكم هذه العلة فيه لمانع ، وهو أن المغصوب لا يحتمل الانتقال فكان هذا تخصيصاً، وهذا باطل. وإنما الصحيح ما قلنا إن الحكم عُدم لعدم العلة، وهو كون الغصب سبباً لملك بدل العين المغصوبة ؛ لأن ضمان المدبّر ليس ببدل عن العين المغصوبة، لكنه بدل عن اليد الفائتة ؛ لما قلنا إنه ليس بمحل للنقل، فالذي جعل عندهم دليل الخصوص: جعلناه دليل العدم، وهذا أصلُ هذا الفصل، فاحفظه وأحكمه، ففيه فقه كثير ، ومَخلَص كبير. و* وإنما يلزم الخصوص على العلل الطردية؛ لأنها قائمة بصيغتها ور والخصوص يَرِدُّ على العبارات، دون المعاني الخالصة. 6 ومن ذلك : قولنا في الزنا إنه يوجب حرمة المصاهرة؛ لأنه حرث للولد، فأُقيم مقامه ، ولما خلق الولد من مائهما، أو اجتمعا على الوطء، وجاءت بينهما شبهة البعضية بواسطة الولد صارت بناتها وأمهاتها كبناته وأمهاته، وآباؤه وأبناؤه كآبائها وأبنائها فلزم على هذا أنه لم تَحرُم الأخوات والعمات والخالات، فقال أهلُ المقالة الأولى إنه مخصوص بالنص، مع قيام العلة. وقلنا : بل العلل صارت عللاً شرعاً، لا بذواتها، وهي لم تُجعل علةً عند معارضة النص، وفي هذا معارضةٌ؛ لأن حكم النص يزداد بامتداد الحرمة إلى الأخوات وغيرهن فلا تبقى علة عند معارضة النص، فيكون عدم الحكم : لعدم العلة. وليس هذا من باب الخصوص في شيء، وهذا واضح جداً. ومن أحكم المعرفة ، وأحسن الطويَّةَ سَهُلَ عليه تخريج الجُمَل على هذا الأصل إن شاء الله تعالى.
And its explanation: in our statement regarding the fasting person when water is poured into his throat: it invalidates his fast because the pillar of fasting has been lost. And it applies to the forgetful person. So whoever allowed specification said: the ruling of this cause is prevented there due to a preventer, which is the trace. And we said: it is prevented due to the absence of this cause, because the act of the forgetful is attributed to the Lawgiver, so the meaning of transgression falls away from him, and the act becomes pardoned, so the fast remains due to the survival of its pillar, not due to a preventer with the loss of its pillar. And similarly our statement regarding usurpation: when it became a cause for ownership of the replacement of property, it must be a cause for ownership of the original. As for the mudabbar slave, the ruling of this cause is prevented in his case due to a preventer, which is that the usurped item does not permit transfer; so this would be specification, and this is false. Rather the correct view is what we said: the ruling is absent due to the absence of the cause, which is that usurpation is a cause for ownership of the replacement of the usurped item, because the guarantee of the mudabbar is not a replacement for the usurped item, but a replacement for the lost possession; because we said it is not a locus for transfer. So what they made a proof of specification, we made a proof of absence. And this is the foundation of this chapter, so memorize it and master it, for in it is much jurisprudence and great deliverance. And specification only applies to formal causes because they are based on their wording, and specification applies to expressions, not to pure meanings. And from that is our statement regarding adultery: it necessitates the prohibition of marriage relations because it is a field for the child, so it stood in its place, and when the child is created from their fluids, or they come together in intercourse, and between them comes a semblance of partiality through the child, her daughters and mothers become like his daughters and mothers, and his fathers and sons become like her fathers and sons. So it follows from this that sisters, aunts, and maternal aunts are not prohibited. Then the proponents of the first opinion said: it is specified by the text, while the cause is valid. And we said: rather, causes become legal causes by revelation, not by themselves, and they are not made causes when they oppose the text. And in this is opposition, because the ruling of the text increases by the extension of prohibition to sisters and others, so the cause does not remain when opposing the text. Thus the absence of ruling is due to absence of cause. And this is not from the category of specification at all, and this is very clear. And whoever masters knowledge and has good intention, it will be easy for him to derive general rulings upon this principle, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 626

Commentary
This passage is a sustained usul dispute defending the Hanafi position that when a ruling derived from an 'illah (legal cause) is absent in a particular case, it is not due to a preventer (mani') that would specify the 'illah (takhsis), but rather due to the absence of the 'illah itself. The author begins with the example of a fasting person—if water is poured into his throat, the fast is invalidated because the pillar (rkn, namely restraint) is lost. However, for a forgetful person who unintentionally swallows water, the fast remains valid. Opponents (ahl al-takhsis) argue that the 'illah (losing the pillar) still exists but is prevented by a trace (athar, i.e., Quranic evidence pardoning forgetfulness). The Hanafis respond that the act of a forgetful person is attributed to the Lawgiver (since the Lawgiver waives punishment), so the act becomes pardoned ('afwan), meaning the 'illah of transgression is absent. Thus the fast remains because its pillar persists—not due to a preventer but because the 'illah is not present. Next, the author discusses ghasb (usurpation). The principle is that usurpation causes ownership of a replacement (badal mal). For a mudabbar slave (one promised freedom after master's death), opponents claim that if a mudabbar is usurped, the guarantee is not ownership of the slave himself (since he cannot be transferred) but compensation for lost possession. They say this specifies the 'illah: usurpation causes ownership of replacement except for non-transferable property. The Hanafis argue that the ruling is absent because the 'illah is different: for the mudabbar, the guarantee is not a replacement for the property but for the lost hand (i.e., possession), so the 'illah of causing ownership of replacement is not present at all. Thus, what opponents considered a proof of specification is actually a proof of absence of 'illah. The author then notes that specification only occurs in formal causes ('ilal tirdiyya) that are based on wording, not in causes based on pure meanings. Finally, the example of zina (adultery) is given: it creates an impediment to marriage (hurmah al-musaharah) because it is a cause for the child. The 'illah is that through the child, a semblance of partiality exists, so the adulterer's daughters and mothers become like his own. However, sisters, aunts, etc., are not prohibited by consensus. Opponents say the 'illah is still valid but is specified by text (i.e., the general rule is narrowed). Hanafis respond that causes are legal ('illa shar'iyya) not by themselves but by being made so by the Lawgiver. When a text explicitly limits the ruling (e.g., prohibiting only specific relatives), the 'illah cannot operate beyond the text's scope; hence the 'illah is not present for the excluded categories. Thus absence of ruling is again due to absence of 'illah, not specification. The author concludes that whoever understands this principle can easily derive rulings from it.

Key Terms
العلة الطردية (al-'illah al-tirdiyyah): A formal cause that is based on linguistic expression; it can be specified by wording.
المعاني الخالصة (al-ma'ani al-khalisah): Pure meanings, not tied to wording; causes based on such meanings cannot be specified.
حرمة المصاهرة (hurmah al-musaharah): Prohibition of marriage due to marriage or illicit relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this lesson, why is a sister of the adulterous partner not prohibited for marriage?
A) Because the 'illah is specified by the text, excluding sisters.
B) Because the 'illah does not exist for sisters; the text defines the scope of the 'illah.
C) Because the 'illah is blocked by a preventer.
D) Because the sister is not a blood relative of the adulterer.

Key Takeaway
Meaning-based causes are defined by the Lawgiver's ruling; absence of ruling indicates absence of the cause, not specification.

Response to Objection on Prohibition via Breastfeeding
Response to objection regarding scope of prohibition via breastfeeding analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on why breastfeeding prohibition does not extend to sisters and aunts, and distinguish between absence of cause and textual specification.

Core Idea
Cause is not operative when text exists; absence of ruling is due to absent cause, not specification.

In usul al-fiqh, a key debate concerns whether qiyas can extend a ruling beyond the literal text. Here, the opponent claims that since the text mentions only specific relatives, analogical extension to sisters and aunts is blocked by takhsis (specification). The Hanafi response, however, reframes the issue: the legal cause (illah) is not inherent but designated by the Lawgiver, and it is not made operative when the text itself covers the case. Thus, the absence of ruling for sisters is not due to a textual exception but because the cause is simply not effective. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The dispute is about whether the prohibition via breastfeeding (ridaa') extends to sisters and aunts beyond the explicitly mentioned relatives.
The opponent says the text is specific, so qiyas is invalid.
2
State the opponent's view
The opponent argues that the text has specified certain relatives, so the cause is effective but the ruling is limited by specification (takhsis).
They say: 'It is makhsus (specific) by the text, despite the existence of the cause.'
3
Explain the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that causes are legal, not inherent. They are only operative when the text does not oppose. Here, the text exists, so the cause is not made a cause; the absence of ruling is due to absence of cause, not specificity.
Key phrase: 'العلل صارت عللاً شرعاً، لا بذواتها' (causes become legal causes, not by themselves).
4
Clarify the distinction
This is not a case of takhsis (specification) but of inoperative cause. The ruling does not extend because the cause is not present (when the text is present).
The passage says: 'وليس هذا من باب الخصوص في شيء' (this is not from the chapter of specification at all).
5
Apply the principle
With this understanding, one can derive other rulings: whenever a text exists that covers certain cases, the cause does not extend beyond them; absence of ruling is due to absence of operative cause, not a textual preventer.
The author concludes that this makes deriving general principles easy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجاءت بينهما شبهة البعضية بواسطة الولد صارت بناتها وأمهاتها كبناته وأمهاته، وآباؤه وأبناؤه كآبائها وأبنائها فلزم على هذا أنه لم تَحرُم الأخوات والعمات والخالات، فقال أهلُ المقالة الأولى إنه مخصوص بالنص، مع قيام العلة. وقلنا : بل العلل صارت عللاً شرعاً، لا بذواتها، وهي لم تُجعل علةً عند معارضة النص، وفي هذا معارضةٌ؛ لأن حكم النص يزداد بامتداد الحرمة إلى الأخوات وغيرهن فلا تبقى علة عند معارضة النص، فيكون عدم الحكم : لعدم العلة. وليس هذا من باب الخصوص في شيء، وهذا واضح جداً. ومن أحكم المعرفة ، وأحسن الطويَّةَ سَهُلَ عليه تخريج الجُمَل على هذا الأصل إن شاء الله تعالى.
And between them came the doubt of partiality through the child, so her daughters and mothers became like his daughters and mothers, and his fathers and sons became like her fathers and sons. So it follows from this that sisters, aunts, and maternal aunts are not prohibited. So the people of the first article said it is specific by the text, despite the existence of the cause. And we said: Rather, the causes become legal causes, not by themselves, and they are not made a cause when the text is opposed. And in this is opposition, because the ruling of the text increases by the extension of prohibition to sisters and others, so the cause does not remain when the text is opposed, so the absence of ruling is due to the absence of cause. And this is not from the chapter of specification at all, and this is very clear. And whoever has firm knowledge and good intention, it will be easy for him to derive the general principles on this basis, God willing.
Source pages p. 627

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection concerning the analogical extension of marriage prohibitions through breastfeeding. The opponent argues that the text (Qur'an or hadith) specifically prohibits certain relations and not sisters, aunts, etc., so the analogy (qiyas) based on the cause (breastfeeding) is invalid because the text is specific. The Hanafi position, presented here, is that the cause is not an inherent quality but is designated by the Lawgiver. When the text is present, the cause is not considered effective; it does not create a prohibition beyond what the text covers. Therefore, the absence of ruling for sisters is not due to specificity (takhsis) but due to the absence of the cause in the presence of the text. This clarifies that the principle of 'illah is not automatically operative when there is a text, and this is not a case of specific exception but of the definition of cause itself. The author concludes that this understanding facilitates deriving further rulings.

Key Terms
علة (‘illa): A legal cause that is designated by the Lawgiver and, when present and not opposed by a text, yields a ruling.
خصوص (khusūs): Specification of a general ruling by a text, limiting its application.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are sisters not prohibited through the breastfeeding analogy?
A) Because the text specifies only certain relations.
B) Because the cause is not present when the text exists.
C) Because there is a preventer (mani‘) that causes specificity.
D) Because the analogy is weak.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between an inoperative cause and textual specification is key to understanding how qiyas interacts with nass.
